Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, and $V_{stadium}$ be the volume of the stadium.
In the $n$-th insertion, $2^{n-1}$ golf balls are inserted.
The total number of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is given by the sum of a geometric series:
$N_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls after $n$ insertions is $V_n = N_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So,
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
Thus, the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 V_{30} = 2 (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $k$ be the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Then, we want to find the smallest integer $k$ such that $V_k \ge V_{stadium}$.
We want to find $n$ such that $V_n = V_{stadium}$.
$(2^n - 1) V_{ball} = V_{stadium} = 2 (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Dividing both sides by $V_{ball}$, we get:
$2^n - 1 = 2 (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^n - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$

We are asked how many insertions are *left* to fill it after the 30th insertion. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion. Then the total number of insertions is $30 + x$.
We need to find $x$ such that $V_{30+x} = V_{stadium}$.
$V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) V_{ball} = V_{stadium} = 2 (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

We need to find an integer $x$ such that $2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$.
Since $2^{31} - 1$ is slightly less than $2^{31}$, we expect $30+x$ to be slightly less than $31$. However, $30+x$ must be an integer.
If we consider integer values for $x$.
If $x=0$, total insertions = 30, volume is $V_{30} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$ (half full).
If $x=1$, total insertions = 31, volume is $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$.
We know $V_{stadium} = 2 (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
So, $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball} > (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly more than full.
Since at 30 insertions the stadium is half full, and at 31 insertions it is slightly over full, it means we need only 1 more insertion to fill the stadium (or slightly overfill it).

The number of insertions left to fill it is $31 - 30 = 1$.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a single golf ball, which is given as $40 \text{cm}^3$.
Let $N_i$ be the number of balls inserted in the $i$-th insertion. We are given that $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $S_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1}$.
This is a geometric series with first term $a=1$, common ratio $r=2$, and $n$ terms. The sum is given by $S_n = \frac{a(r^n - 1)}{r-1} = \frac{1(2^n - 1)}{2-1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

$V_{30} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
So, $\frac{1}{2} V_{stadium} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$

$(2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

$2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$.

The total number of insertions would be $30 + 1 = 31$.

We want to check if $V_{31} = V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

$V_{31}$ is slightly larger than $V_{stadium}$. However, the question asks how many insertions are *left* to fill it, implying when it becomes full or just exceeds the full volume.

Since $2^{30} V_{ball} > (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$, one more insertion (the 31st insertion) will be enough to fill the stadium (and slightly overfill it).

Let $V$ be the volume of the stadium and $v = 40 cm^3$ be the volume of a golf ball.
After 30 insertions, the stadium is half full. The number of balls inserted after 30 insertions is $\sum_{i=1}^{30} 2^{i-1} = 2^{30} - 1$.

$(2^n - 1)v = V = (2^{31} - 2)v$.

$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$.

Full volume of stadium $V = (2^{31} - 2) \times 40$.
We can see that the volume after 31 insertions, $(2^{31} - 1) \times 40$, is greater than the full volume $V = (2^{31} - 2) \times 40$.

In the next insertion, the 31st insertion, we add $2^{31-1} = 2^{30}$ balls.
Volume added in the 31st insertion = $2^{30} \times 40$.
Since $2^{30} \times 40 > (2^{30} - 1) \times 40$, the volume added in the 31st insertion is more than the remaining volume.
Therefore, we need only 1 more insertion to fill the stadium.

The number of balls inserted in the $i$-th insertion is $2^{i-1}$.

So, the volume of golf balls inserted in the $i$-th insertion is $2^{i-1} v$.
The total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = \sum_{i=1}^n 2^{i-1} v = v \sum_{i=1}^n 2^{i-1} = v (1 + 2 + 4 + \cdots + 2^{n-1}) = v (2^n - 1)$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
So, $V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) v = \frac{1}{2} V$, where $V$ is the total volume of the stadium.
Thus, $V = 2 V_{30} = 2 (2^{30} - 1) v = (2^{31} - 2) v$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely, starting from the state after 30 insertions. Let $k$ be the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium.
We need to find the smallest integer $k$ such that after $30+k$ insertions, the volume of golf balls is at least $V$.
The volume of golf balls after $30+k$ insertions is $V_{30+k} = (2^{30+k} - 1) v$.
We want to find the smallest $k$ such that $V_{30+k} \ge V$.
$(2^{30+k} - 1) v \ge (2^{31} - 2) v$.
$2^{30+k} - 1 \ge 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^{30+k} \ge 2^{31} - 1$.
We want to find the smallest integer $k$ that satisfies this inequality.
If $k=1$, then $2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$.
Since $2^{31} > 2^{31} - 1$, the inequality $2^{30+k} \ge 2^{31} - 1$ is satisfied for $k=1$.
If $k=0$, then $2^{30+0} = 2^{30}$.
We need to check if $2^{30} \ge 2^{31} - 1$.
$2^{30} < 2^{31} - 1$ because $2^{31} - 2^{30} = 2^{30} > 1$.
So, $k=0$ does not work. The smallest integer $k$ that works is $k=1$.
Therefore, we need 1 more insertion to fill the stadium after the 30th insertion.
The number of insertions left to fill it is 1.

Total number of balls after $n$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:

$V_N = (2^N - 1) \cdot V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$.

$(2^N - 1) \cdot V_{ball} = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1) \cdot V_{ball}$.

$2^N - 1 = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^N - 1 = 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2$

$2^N = 2^{31} - 1$

If we assume $N = 31$, then $2^{31} - 1 = 2^{31} - 1$.
So, $N = 31$ is the total number of insertions to fill the stadium.
Number of insertions left = $N - 30 = 31 - 30 = 1$.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, which is approximately $40 cm^3$.
Let $N_i$ be the number of balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion, where $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is the sum of the balls inserted in each insertion from 1 to $k$:
$$ \sum_{i=1}^{k} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{k} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{k-1} $$
This is a geometric series with first term $a = 1$, common ratio $r = 2$, and $k$ terms. The sum of this geometric series is given by:
$$ S_k = \frac{a(r^k - 1)}{r - 1} = \frac{1(2^k - 1)}{2 - 1} = 2^k - 1 $$
So, the total number of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $2^k - 1$.
The total volume of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $V_k = (2^k - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium. Then, the volume of balls after 30 insertions is half of the stadium volume:
$$ V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium} $$
From this, we can find the total volume of the stadium:
$$ V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} $$

We want to find out how many more insertions are needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion. So, we are looking at the $(30+x)$-th insertion in total to fill the stadium. The volume of balls after $(30+x)$ insertions should be equal to the stadium volume:
$$ V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium} $$
Substituting the expression for $V_{stadium}$:
$$ (2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} $$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$$ 2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) $$
$$ 2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2 $$
$$ 2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2 $$
Add 1 to both sides:
$$ 2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1 $$
$$ 2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1 $$
If we consider that $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate:
$$ 2^{30+x} \approx 2^{31} $$
$$ 30+x \approx 31 $$
$$ x \approx 1 $$
Let's check if $x=1$ is exactly correct.
If $x=1$, then total insertions = $30+1=31$.
Volume after 31 insertions = $(2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
Stadium volume $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.
Comparing volume after 31 insertions and stadium volume:
Volume after 31 insertions = $(2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
Stadium volume = $(2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$
Since $2^{31} - 1 > 2^{31} - 2$, the volume after 31 insertions is slightly greater than the stadium volume.
However, we are asked how many insertions are *left* to fill it when it is half full at 30th insertion.
Since one more insertion makes the volume exceed the full volume, it means just 1 more insertion is needed to fill it.

$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let V be the total volume of the stadium.
Let $V_n$ be the volume occupied by golf balls after the $n$-th insertion.
The number of golf balls inserted in each step forms a geometric progression: $1, 2, 4, 8, \dots, 2^{n-1}$ in the $n$-th insertion.
The total number of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of this geometric series:
$N_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \sum_{i=0}^{n-1} 2^i = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
The volume occupied by these golf balls is $V_n = N_n \times 40 = (2^n - 1) \times 40$ cm$^3$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times 40 = \frac{V}{2}$.
So, the full volume of the stadium is $V = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times 40 = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times 40 = (2^{31} - 2) \times 40$ cm$^3$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let's say it takes $k$ insertions to fill the stadium. Then the volume occupied after $k$ insertions is $V_k = V$.
$V_k = (2^k - 1) \times 40 = V = (2^{31} - 2) \times 40$.
Divide both sides by 40:
$2^k - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^k = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^k = 2^{31} - 1$.

We want to find how many more insertions are needed after the 30th insertion to fill the stadium. Let $m$ be the number of additional insertions needed. So, the total number of insertions will be $30 + m$. We want to find $m$ such that $V_{30+m} = V$.
$V_{30+m} = (2^{30+m} - 1) \times 40 = V = (2^{31} - 2) \times 40$.
$2^{30+m} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^{30+m} = 2^{31} - 1$.

Since $2^{30+m} = 2^{31} - 1$, and $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate $30+m \approx 31$, which means $m \approx 1$.
Let's check for $m=1$. Total insertions = $30+1 = 31$.
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times 40$.
$V = (2^{31} - 2) \times 40$.
$V_{31} - V = ((2^{31} - 1) - (2^{31} - 2)) \times 40 = (2^{31} - 1 - 2^{31} + 2) \times 40 = 1 \times 40 = 40$.
After 31 insertions, the stadium is overfilled by the volume of one golf ball.
Since at 30th insertion, the stadium is half full, and at 31st insertion, it is slightly over full, it means that just 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let V be the total volume of the stadium.
Let v be the volume of a golf ball, which is given as 40 cm^3.
In each insertion, the number of golf balls inserted doubles.
The number of balls inserted in each insertion follows a geometric progression:
Insertion 1: 2^(1-1) = 1 ball
Insertion 2: 2^(2-1) = 2 balls
Insertion 3: 2^(3-1) = 4 balls
...
Insertion n: 2^(n-1) balls

The total number of balls inserted after n insertions is the sum of this geometric series:
Total balls after n insertions = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^(n-1) = $\sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$

The total volume of golf balls inserted after n insertions is:
Volume after n insertions = (2^n - 1) * v

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
Volume after 30 insertions = (2^30 - 1) * v = V/2

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely, which means the volume should be V. Let N be the number of insertions required to fill the stadium.
Volume after N insertions = (2^N - 1) * v = V

From the information given at the 30th insertion:
V = 2 * (Volume after 30 insertions) = 2 * (2^30 - 1) * v = (2 * 2^30 - 2) * v = (2^31 - 2) * v

Now we set the volume after N insertions equal to V:
(2^N - 1) * v = (2^31 - 2) * v

Divide both sides by v:
2^N - 1 = 2^31 - 2
2^N = 2^31 - 2 + 1
2^N = 2^31 - 1

We want to find the number of *additional* insertions needed after the 30th insertion. Let's consider what happens at the next insertion, i.e., the 31st insertion.
Volume after 31 insertions = (2^31 - 1) * v

Comparing this with V = (2^31 - 2) * v, we can see that the volume after 31 insertions, (2^31 - 1) * v, is slightly larger than V/2 at 30th insertion, (2^30 - 1) * v, and very close to V = 2 * (2^30 - 1) * v.

Let's approximate. For large numbers, $2^n - 1 \approx 2^n$.
Volume after 30 insertions $\approx 2^{30} * v = V/2$.
V $\approx 2 * 2^{30} * v = 2^{31} * v$.
Volume after N insertions $\approx 2^N * v = V \approx 2^{31} * v$.
This implies N = 31.

The number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion is N - 30 = 31 - 30 = 1.

At insertion 30, stadium is half full. To become full, the volume needs to be doubled.
In each insertion, the volume added approximately doubles the current total volume.
So, one more insertion should be enough to fill the remaining half.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?1?Let $V$ be the total volume of the stadium and $v = 40 \text{ cm}^3$ be the volume of a single golf ball.
In the $n$-th insertion, the number of golf balls inserted is $2^{n-1}$.
The total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is given by the sum of the volumes inserted in each step:
$V_n = (1 \cdot v) + (2 \cdot v) + (4 \cdot v) + \dots + (2^{n-1} \cdot v)$
$V_n = v \cdot (1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1})$
The sum $1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1}$ is a geometric series with first term $a = 1$, common ratio $r = 2$, and $n$ terms. The sum of this geometric series is given by $\frac{a(r^n - 1)}{r - 1} = \frac{1(2^n - 1)}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
So, $V_n = v \cdot (2^n - 1)$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means $V_{30} = \frac{1}{2}V$.
$V_{30} = v \cdot (2^{30} - 1) = \frac{1}{2}V$
From this, we can find the total volume of the stadium $V$:
$V = 2 \cdot v \cdot (2^{30} - 1)$

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $N$ be the number of insertions required to fill the stadium. Then $V_N = V$.
$V_N = v \cdot (2^N - 1) = V$
Substitute the expression for $V$:
$v \cdot (2^N - 1) = 2 \cdot v \cdot (2^{30} - 1)$
Divide both sides by $v$:
$2^N - 1 = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^N - 1 = 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2$
$2^N - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^N = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^N = 2^{31} - 1$

We want to find how many insertions are left after the 30th insertion to fill the stadium. Let $x$ be the number of insertions left. Then the total number of insertions is $N = 30 + x$. We want to find $x = N - 30$.
Since $2^N = 2^{31} - 1$, we can see that $N$ is very close to 31. In fact, if we consider the next insertion after the 30th, which is the 31st insertion, the volume added in the 31st insertion is $2^{31-1} \cdot v = 2^{30} \cdot v$.
The volume remaining to fill after 30 insertions is $V - V_{30} = V - \frac{1}{2}V = \frac{1}{2}V = V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v$.
The volume added in the 31st insertion is $2^{30} \cdot v$.
Since $2^{30} \cdot v > (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v$, the volume added in the 31st insertion is greater than the remaining volume needed to fill the stadium. Thus, just 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.
Therefore, the number of insertions left is 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, given as $V_{ball} = 40 \text{cm}^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
In the $i$-th insertion, the number of balls inserted is $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $S_n = \sum_{i=1}^n N_i = \sum_{i=1}^n 2^{i-1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So, the volume of balls after 30 insertions is half the volume of the stadium:
$V_{30} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
From this, we can find the total volume of the stadium:
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $n$ be the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Then the volume of balls after $n$ insertions should be equal to the volume of the stadium:
$V_n = V_{stadium}$
$(2^n - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$.
We are looking for an integer $n$ that satisfies this equation. Since $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate $n \approx 31$.
If $n = 31$, then $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
Comparing $V_{31}$ with $V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$, we see that $V_{31} > V_{stadium}$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled.
However, we are asked "how many insertions are left to fill it" when the stadium is half full at the 30th insertion.
Since at 30th insertion the stadium is half full, we need to fill the remaining half.
We found that 31 insertions are enough to fill (and slightly overfill) the stadium.
So, starting from the 30th insertion, we need $31 - 30 = 1$ more insertion to fill the stadium.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, $V_{ball} = 40 cm^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the volume of the stadium.
In the $i$-th insertion, $2^{i-1}$ golf balls are inserted.
The total number of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is given by the sum of the geometric series:
$S_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) V_{ball}$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So,
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
From this, we can find the full volume of the stadium:
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $k$ be the total number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Then the volume of golf balls after $k$ insertions should be equal to the stadium volume:
$V_k = (2^k - 1) V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$.
$(2^k - 1) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^k - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^k = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^k = 2^{31} - 1$.

We need to find an integer $k$ that satisfies this equation. Since $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate $k \approx 31$. Let's check if $k = 31$:
For $k=31$, the volume is $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$.
We want to check if $V_{31} = V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
We can see that $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$ is slightly greater than $V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
However, we are asked for the number of insertions *left* to fill it, starting from the 30th insertion.
Since at the 30th insertion the stadium is half full, we need to add the remaining half volume.
After 30 insertions, we perform one more insertion, which is the 31st insertion. In the 31st insertion, we add $2^{31-1} = 2^{30}$ balls.
The volume added in the 31st insertion is $2^{30} V_{ball}$.
The remaining volume to fill after the 30th insertion is $\frac{1}{2} V_{stadium} = V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Since $2^{30} V_{ball} > (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$, one more insertion (the 31st insertion) is enough to fill the stadium. In fact, it slightly overfills it.
Therefore, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium after the 30th insertion.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?1?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the volume of the stadium.
Let $N_i$ be the number of golf balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion, where $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $S_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means that the total volume of golf balls after 30 insertions is half of the stadium's volume:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$.
The total volume of golf balls after $30 + x$ insertions is $V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
For the stadium to be full, we need $V_{30+x} = V_{stadium}$.
$(2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

We want to find an integer $x$ that satisfies this equation. Let's test integer values for $x$.
If $x = 1$, then $2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$.
$2^{31} = 2^{31} - 1$ is false. However, $2^{31} > 2^{31} - 1$. This means that if we take $x=1$, then $V_{30+1} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball} > (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$.
So, after 1 additional insertion, the stadium is slightly overfilled. Since we are asked for the number of insertions left to fill it, and we just reached or exceeded the full volume with one more insertion, the answer must be 1.

If we consider the question as "how many more insertions are needed to make it at least full", then 1 insertion is sufficient.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_k$ be the total volume of golf balls after $k$ insertions. The number of balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion is $2^{i-1}$. The total number of balls after $k$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$$N_k = \sum_{i=1}^{k} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + 2^2 + \dots + 2^{k-1} = \frac{2^k - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^k - 1$$
The volume of each golf ball is $V_{ball} = 40 \text{cm}^3$. So, the total volume of golf balls after $k$ insertions is:
$$V_k = N_k \times V_{ball} = (2^k - 1) \times V_{ball}$$
We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium. Then, at the 30th insertion, the volume of golf balls is $\frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
$$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$$
From this, we can find the total volume of the stadium:
$$V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$$
We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium. Let $n$ be the number of additional insertions. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + n$. We want to find $n$ such that the volume of golf balls after $30 + n$ insertions is equal to the volume of the stadium:
$$V_{30+n} = (2^{30+n} - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$$
Substitute the expression for $V_{stadium}$:
$$(2^{30+n} - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$$2^{30+n} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$$
$$2^{30+n} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$$
$$2^{30+n} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$$
$$2^{30+n} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$$
$$2^{30+n} = 2^{31} - 1$$
We are looking for an integer $n$. Let's test $n=1$.
If $n=1$, then total insertions = $30+1 = 31$.
Volume after 31 insertions is $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.
Comparing $V_{31}$ and $V_{stadium}$:
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
$V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$
$V_{31} > V_{stadium}$.
So, at the 31st insertion, the stadium becomes filled (and slightly overfilled if we consider exact fill to capacity). Since we are asked "how many insertions are left to fill it", and at 30th insertion it is half full, it will take only 1 more insertion to fill it.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, which is given as $40 cm^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
Let $N_i$ be the number of golf balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion.
We are given that the number of balls inserted doubles with each insertion, starting with 1 ball in the first insertion. So, $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.

The total number of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$S_k = \sum_{i=1}^{k} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{k} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{k-1}$
This is a geometric series with first term $a = 1$, common ratio $r = 2$, and $k$ terms. The sum is given by:
$S_k = \frac{a(r^k - 1)}{r - 1} = \frac{1(2^k - 1)}{2 - 1} = 2^k - 1$

The total volume of golf balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $V_k = S_k \times V_{ball} = (2^k - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means that the volume of balls inserted after 30 insertions is half of the stadium's volume:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$
So, the full volume of the stadium is:
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$

We want to find out how many more insertions are needed to fill the stadium completely after the 30th insertion. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$. The total volume of balls inserted after $30 + x$ insertions is:
$V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball}$

For the stadium to be full, $V_{30+x}$ must be equal to $V_{stadium}$:
$(2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

Let's consider the volume added at each step. At the 30th insertion, the stadium is half full. We need to fill the remaining half. The volume added at the 31st insertion is $N_{31} \times V_{ball} = 2^{31-1} \times V_{ball} = 2^{30} \times V_{ball}$.
The remaining volume to fill is half of the stadium volume, which is $V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
Since $2^{30} > 2^{30} - 1$, the volume added at the 31st insertion is greater than the remaining volume. This means that after the 31st insertion, the stadium will be full (or even overfull, but we consider filling it to capacity).
Therefore, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium after the 30th insertion.
The number of insertions left is $31 - 30 = 1$.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, $V_{ball} = 40 cm^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
The number of balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion is $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $S_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2-1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) V_{ball}$.

$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
Thus, $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Let $m$ be the total number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Then, the volume of balls at $m$-th insertion should be equal to the volume of the stadium:
$V_m = (2^m - 1) V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$.
Substitute the expression for $V_{stadium}$:
$(2^m - 1) V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^m - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$.
$2^m - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$.
$2^m - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^m = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^m = 2^{31} - 1$.

We want to find the number of insertions left after the 30th insertion to fill the stadium. Let $k$ be the number of insertions left. Then $m = 30 + k$.
$2^{30+k} = 2^{31} - 1$.
Since $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate $2^{30+k} \approx 2^{31}$, which gives $30+k \approx 31$, so $k \approx 1$.

Let's check for $k=1$. If we have $30+1 = 31$ insertions, the volume is $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$.
We know $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
Comparing $V_{31}$ and $V_{stadium}$:
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$
$V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$
Since $2^{31} - 1 > 2^{31} - 2$, we have $V_{31} > V_{stadium}$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled. However, since at 30 insertions it is exactly half full and the volume approximately doubles with each step, it is reasonable to assume that only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Number of insertions left = $m - 30 \approx 1$.
Since we are asked for the number that solves the problem, and 1 is the closest integer, and after 1 more insertion the stadium is filled or slightly overfilled for the first time after being half full, the answer should be 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, $V_{ball} = 40 cm^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the volume of the stadium.
Let $N_i$ be the number of balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion, $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $T_k = \sum_{i=1}^{k} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{k} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + \dots + 2^{k-1} = \frac{2^k - 1}{2-1} = 2^k - 1$.
The total volume of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $V_k = T_k \times V_{ball} = (2^k - 1) V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
So, $V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
This means the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Let $n$ be the total number of insertions to fill the stadium. Then the volume of balls after $n$ insertions should be equal to the volume of the stadium.
$V_n = (2^n - 1) V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$
$(2^n - 1) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$

We are asked for the number of insertions *left* to fill it after the 30th insertion. Let $x$ be the number of insertions left. Then the total number of insertions is $30 + x = n$.
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$
If we consider integer values for $x$, we observe that if $x=1$, then $30+x=31$, and $2^{31} = 2^{31}$.
$2^{31}$ is very close to $2^{31} - 1$.
In fact, if we consider the number of balls at each insertion, we can see that by going from the 30th insertion to the 31st, the number of balls added is $2^{30}$.
The number of balls already in the stadium after 30 insertions is $2^{30} - 1$.
The volume at 30th insertion is half the stadium volume.
In the 31st insertion, we add $2^{30}$ balls, which has a volume of $2^{30} V_{ball}$.
The remaining volume to fill is also $(2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Since $2^{30} > 2^{30} - 1$, adding one more insertion is enough to fill the remaining volume and even slightly overfill it.
However, if we are looking for the exact number of insertions to reach the volume $V_{stadium}$, and based on $2^n = 2^{31} - 1$, there is no integer $n$ that satisfies this exactly.

Given the context and the doubling nature, it is most likely that "fill it" means to reach or exceed the full volume for the first time after being exactly half full at the 30th insertion.
Since adding one more insertion (31st insertion) adds a volume of $2^{30} V_{ball}$ which is greater than the remaining volume of $(2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$, one more insertion is sufficient to fill the stadium.
Therefore, the number of insertions left to fill it is 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V$ be the total volume of the stadium.
Let $v$ be the volume of a single golf ball, $v = 40 \, \text{cm}^3$.
In the $n$-th insertion, we insert $2^{n-1}$ golf balls.
The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $N_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \sum_{i=0}^{n-1} 2^i = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume occupied by the golf balls after $n$ insertions is $V_n = N_n \times v = (2^n - 1)v$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means that the volume occupied by the golf balls after 30 insertions is half of the total volume of the stadium.
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1)v = \frac{V}{2}$.
Therefore, the total volume of the stadium is $V = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)v$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $m$ be the total number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Then the volume occupied by the golf balls after $m$ insertions should be equal to the total volume of the stadium $V$.
$V_m = (2^m - 1)v = V$.
Substituting the expression for $V$:
$(2^m - 1)v = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)v$.
Divide both sides by $v$:
$2^m - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$.
$2^m - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$.
$2^m - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^m = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^m = 2^{31} - 1$.

We want to find how many insertions are left after the 30th insertion to fill the stadium. Let $k$ be the number of insertions left. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + k$. We need to find the smallest integer $k$ such that the stadium is filled after $30+k$ insertions.
We need to find the smallest integer $k$ such that $V_{30+k} \ge V$.
$V_{30+k} = (2^{30+k} - 1)v \ge V = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)v$.
$2^{30+k} - 1 \ge 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$.
$2^{30+k} - 1 \ge 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^{30+k} \ge 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^{30+k} \ge 2^{31} - 1$.
For $k=1$, $2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$. Is $2^{31} \ge 2^{31} - 1$ Yes, it is true.
For $k=0$, $2^{30+0} = 2^{30}$. Is $2^{30} \ge 2^{31} - 1$ No, $2^{30} < 2^{31} - 1$.
So the smallest integer value for $k$ is 1.
Therefore, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?Let V_ball be the volume of a golf ball, which is approximately 40 cm^3.
Let V_stadium be the total volume of the stadium.
The number of golf balls inserted at each insertion follows a geometric progression:
Insertion 1: 1 ball
Insertion 2: 2 balls
Insertion 3: 4 balls
...
Insertion n: 2^(n-1) balls

The total number of balls inserted after n insertions is the sum of this geometric series:
S_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^(n-1) = (2^n - 1) / (2 - 1) = 2^n - 1

The total volume of golf balls inserted after n insertions is V_n = S_n * V_ball = (2^n - 1) * V_ball.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means:
V_30 = (2^30 - 1) * V_ball = 0.5 * V_stadium

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let x be the number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion. So we are looking for the number of insertions n = 30 + x such that the stadium is full, i.e., V_n = V_stadium.
V_(30+x) = (2^(30+x) - 1) * V_ball = V_stadium

From the information at the 30th insertion, we know V_stadium = 2 * V_30 = 2 * (2^30 - 1) * V_ball.
So we set V_(30+x) = V_stadium:
(2^(30+x) - 1) * V_ball = 2 * (2^30 - 1) * V_ball

Divide both sides by V_ball:
2^(30+x) - 1 = 2 * (2^30 - 1)
2^(30+x) - 1 = 2 * 2^30 - 2
2^(30+x) = 2 * 2^30 - 1
2^(30+x) = 2^(31) - 1

We are looking for an integer x. If we approximate -1 to be negligible compared to 2^31 for large numbers, we can approximate:
2^(30+x)  2^(31)
30 + x  31
x  1

Let's check if x = 1 is the exact integer answer in the context of the problem.
If we have 1 more insertion after the 30th, we go to the 31st insertion.
Volume at 31st insertion is V_31 = (2^31 - 1) * V_ball = (2 * 2^30 - 1) * V_ball = (2 * 2^30 - 2 + 1) * V_ball = (2 * (2^30 - 1) + 1) * V_ball = 2 * (2^30 - 1) * V_ball + 1 * V_ball = V_stadium + V_ball.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled by the volume of one golf ball. However, since at 30 insertions it is half full, the volume roughly doubles with each insertion. Thus, one more insertion should be sufficient to fill the remaining half.

The question asks "how many insertions are left to fill it". Since at 30th insertion the stadium is exactly half full, and with each subsequent insertion the volume added is roughly equal to the current volume (for large insertion number), it is reasonable to assume that just one more insertion will fill the remaining half and possibly slightly overfill it, but that's the closest integer number of insertions to fill it. Given the phrasing and the exponential growth, it must be exactly 1 more insertion to go from half full to full (or slightly over).

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, where $V_{ball} = 40 \text{cm}^3$.
Let $N_i$ be the number of balls inserted in the $i$-th insertion, where $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $S_k = \sum_{i=1}^k N_i = \sum_{i=1}^k 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + \dots + 2^{k-1} = \frac{2^k - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^k - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls after $k$ insertions is $V_k = S_k \times V_{ball} = (2^k - 1) V_{ball}$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. Let $V_{stadium}$ be the volume of the stadium.
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
So, $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium. Let $n$ be the number of additional insertions. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + n$.
The volume after $30 + n$ insertions is $V_{30+n} = (2^{30+n} - 1) V_{ball}$.
We want to find $n$ such that $V_{30+n} = V_{stadium}$.
$(2^{30+n} - 1) V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+n} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+n} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+n} = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+n} = 2 \times 2^{30} - 1$
$2^{30+n} = 2^{31} - 1$

We want to find an integer $n$ that satisfies this equation.
Let's test $n=1$:
$2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$.
$2^{31} - 1 \approx 2^{31}$.
So, $2^{30+n} = 2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{30+n} = 2^{31}$, which gives $30+n = 31$, so $n=1$.

Let's check if $n=1$ makes the stadium full or slightly overfull.
For $n=1$, the number of insertions is $30+1 = 31$.
Volume after 31 insertions is $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Stadium volume is $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
Comparing $V_{31}$ and $V_{stadium}$:
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$
$V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$
$V_{31} > V_{stadium}$.
So, after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled.
Since at 30 insertions it is half full, and at 31 insertions it is overfull, it means that just 1 more insertion is needed to go from half full to filled.
Therefore, there is 1 insertion left to fill the stadium.

$$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$$
$$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$$

The total volume of golf balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $V_k = S_k \times V_{ball} = (2^k - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means that the volume of golf balls after 30 insertions is half of the stadium's volume:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$
So, the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find out how many more insertions are needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$. The volume of golf balls after $30+x$ insertions should be equal to the stadium volume:
$V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$
Substitute the expression for $V_{stadium}$:
$(2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

We want to find an integer $x$. Let's check for $x=1$:
If $x=1$, then $30+x = 31$.
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$
Comparing $V_{31}$ and $V_{stadium}$:
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
$V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$
Since $2^{31} - 1 > 2^{31} - 2$, we have $V_{31} > V_{stadium}$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled.
However, at 30 insertions it is half full. Thus, just one more insertion is needed to fill it.

Number of insertions left = 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Rationale:
Let $V$ be the volume of a single golf ball. Let $S$ be the total volume of the stadium.
In the $n$-th insertion, $2^{n-1}$ golf balls are inserted.
The total number of golf balls inserted after $k$ insertions is given by the sum of a geometric series:
$N_k = \sum_{i=1}^{k} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + \dots + 2^{k-1} = \frac{2^k - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^k - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $V_k = N_k \times V = (2^k - 1)V$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means that the volume of golf balls after 30 insertions is half the stadium volume:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1)V = \frac{1}{2}S$.
From this, we can find the total volume of the stadium:
$S = 2V_{30} = 2(2^{30} - 1)V$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$. The volume of golf balls after $30 + x$ insertions should be equal to the stadium volume $S$:
$V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1)V = S$.
Substituting the expression for $S$:
$(2^{30+x} - 1)V = 2(2^{30} - 1)V$.
Divide both sides by $V$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2(2^{30} - 1)$.
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$.
$2^{30+x} = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2 + 1$.
$2^{30+x} = 2 \times 2^{30} - 1$.
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$.

If we consider $x=1$, then the total number of insertions is $30+1 = 31$.
The volume of golf balls after 31 insertions is $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1)V$.
We need to check if $V_{31} = S$.
$S = 2(2^{30} - 1)V = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2)V = (2^{31} - 2)V$.
Comparing $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1)V$ and $S = (2^{31} - 2)V$, we see that $V_{31} > S$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled.

However, we need to find how many insertions are *left* to fill it, meaning from the point when it is half full, how many more insertions are needed to reach full capacity. Since at 30 insertions it is half full, and at 31 insertions it becomes more than full, it means only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium (or slightly overfill, which in practical terms means filled).

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let V be the total volume of the stadium.
Let v be the volume of a single golf ball, which is approximately 40 cm^3.
In each insertion, the number of golf balls inserted doubles. The number of balls inserted in each insertion follows a geometric progression:
Insertion 1: 1 ball
Insertion 2: 2 balls
Insertion 3: 4 balls
...
Insertion n: 2^(n-1) balls

The total volume of golf balls inserted after n insertions is the sum of the volumes of balls inserted in each step. The total number of balls after n insertions is the sum of the geometric series:
Total balls after n insertions = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^(n-1) = 2^n - 1.
The total volume of golf balls after n insertions is (2^n - 1) * v.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means that the volume of golf balls after 30 insertions is V/2.
V/2 = (2^30 - 1) * v

We want to find out how many more insertions are needed to fill the stadium completely. Let x be the number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion to fill the stadium. So, we are looking for the number of insertions required to reach volume V.
From V/2 = (2^30 - 1) * v, we can find the full volume of the stadium V:
V = 2 * (2^30 - 1) * v = (2 * 2^30 - 2) * v = (2^31 - 2) * v

Let N be the total number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. The volume after N insertions must be equal to V.
(2^N - 1) * v = V
(2^N - 1) * v = (2^31 - 2) * v

Divide both sides by v:
2^N - 1 = 2^31 - 2
2^N = 2^31 - 2 + 1
2^N = 2^31 - 1

We are looking for an integer N that satisfies this equation. We can see that if N = 31, then 2^31 - 1 is very close to 2^31.
Let's check the volume after 31 insertions:
Volume after 31 insertions = (2^31 - 1) * v

Compare this to V = (2^31 - 2) * v.
Since (2^31 - 1) * v > (2^31 - 2) * v = V, it means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled or exactly filled (if we interpret "fill it" as at least full).
Since at 30 insertions it is half full, and at 31 insertions it is full (or more), it means that exactly one more insertion is needed to go from half full to full.
Number of insertions left to fill it = 31 - 30 = 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let V be the volume of the stadium, and v be the volume of a golf ball (v = 40 cm^3).
The number of golf balls inserted in each insertion follows a geometric progression: 1, 2, 4, 8, ... where the n-th insertion adds 2^(n-1) balls.
The total number of balls inserted after n insertions is the sum of this geometric series:
Sum of balls after n insertions = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^(n-1) = (2^n - 1) / (2 - 1) = 2^n - 1.
The total volume of golf balls inserted after n insertions is (2^n - 1) * v.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. Let V_30 be the volume filled after 30 insertions.
V_30 = (2^30 - 1) * v = V/2.

We want to find out how many more insertions are needed to fill the stadium completely. Let's consider the volume after 31 insertions, V_31.
V_31 = (2^31 - 1) * v.
We can rewrite 2^31 - 1 as 2 * 2^30 - 1 = 2 * (2^30 - 1) + 2 - 1 = 2 * (2^30 - 1) + 1.
So, V_31 = [2 * (2^30 - 1) + 1] * v = 2 * (2^30 - 1) * v + 1 * v = 2 * V_30 + v.
Since V_30 = V/2, we have V_31 = 2 * (V/2) + v = V + v.

This means that after the 31st insertion, the total volume of golf balls is V + v, which is greater than the stadium volume V (as v > 0).
Since at the 30th insertion the stadium is half full, and at the 31st insertion the stadium is more than full, it means that only one additional insertion (the 31st insertion) is needed to fill the stadium (and in fact, it will overfill it).
Therefore, the number of insertions left to fill the stadium after the 30th insertion is 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball.

$2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$.
Is $2^{31} \ge 2^{31} - 1$ Yes, $2^{31} > 2^{31} - 1$.

So, $x = 0$ is not sufficient.

The smallest integer $x$ that satisfies the inequality is $x = 1$.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let V be the total volume of the stadium.
Let v be the volume of a single golf ball, v = 40 cm^3.
In the n-th insertion, the number of golf balls inserted is $2^{n-1}$.
The total volume of golf balls inserted after n insertions is given by the sum of the volumes inserted in each step:
$V_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} (\text{number of balls in i-th insertion}) \times v = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} \times v = v \times \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = v \times (1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{n-1})$.
This is a geometric series with first term $a = 1$, common ratio $r = 2$, and n terms. The sum of this geometric series is $\frac{a(r^n - 1)}{r - 1} = \frac{1(2^n - 1)}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
So, $V_n = (2^n - 1) \times v$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means $V_{30} = \frac{1}{2}V$.
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times v = \frac{1}{2}V$.
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is $V = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times v$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let's say it takes $n_{full}$ insertions to fill the stadium. Then $V_{n_{full}} = V$.
$V_{n_{full}} = (2^{n_{full}} - 1) \times v = V = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times v$.
Divide both sides by v:
$2^{n_{full}} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{n_{full}} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{n_{full}} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{n_{full}} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{n_{full}} = 2^{31} - 1$

Alternatively, consider the volume remaining to be filled after the 30th insertion. Since the stadium is half full at the 30th insertion, the remaining volume to be filled is also $V/2 = V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times v$.
In the next insertion (31st insertion), the volume of golf balls inserted is $2^{31-1} \times v = 2^{30} \times v$.
Since $2^{30} \times v > (2^{30} - 1) \times v$, the volume inserted in the 31st insertion is greater than the remaining volume needed to fill the stadium.
Therefore, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium completely after the 30th insertion.

Number of insertions left = $n_{full} - 30$.
From the reasoning above, $n_{full} = 31$.
Number of insertions left = $31 - 30 = 1$.

$2^{30+x} \ge 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^{30+x} \ge 2^{31} - 1$.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, which is approximately $40 cm^3$.

Insertion 1: $2^{1-1} = 1$ ball
Insertion 2: $2^{2-1} = 2$ balls
Insertion 3: $2^{3-1} = 4$ balls
...
Insertion n: $2^{n-1}$ balls

The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$S_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$

The total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means that the volume of golf balls after 30 insertions is half of the stadium volume:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$

From this, we can find the total volume of the stadium:
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $N$ be the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Then the volume of golf balls after $N$ insertions should be equal to the stadium volume:
$V_N = (2^N - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$

Substitute the expression for $V_{stadium}$:
$(2^N - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$

Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^N - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^N = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^N = 2^{31} - 1$

We are asked for the number of insertions *left* to fill the stadium after the 30th insertion. Let $x$ be the number of insertions left. Then the total number of insertions to fill the stadium is $N = 30 + x$.
We need to find $x$ such that after $30+x$ insertions, the stadium is full.
We know that after 30 insertions, the stadium is half full. We need to double the volume to fill the stadium.
In the next insertion (31st insertion), the number of balls inserted is $2^{31-1} = 2^{30}$.
The volume added in the 31st insertion is $2^{30} \times V_{ball}$.
The remaining volume to fill after 30 insertions is $\frac{1}{2} V_{stadium} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
Since $2^{30} \times V_{ball} > (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$, the 31st insertion will fill the remaining volume (and even slightly overfill it, but we consider filling it).

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, $V_{ball} = 40 cm^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
In the $i$-th insertion, the number of balls inserted is $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $S_k = \sum_{i=1}^{k} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{k} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + \dots + 2^{k-1} = 2^k - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls after $k$ insertions is $V_k = S_k \times V_{ball} = (2^k - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So, the volume of golf balls after 30 insertions is half of the stadium volume:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
Thus, the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$.
The total volume of golf balls after $30 + x$ insertions is $V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
For the stadium to be full, we must have $V_{30+x} = V_{stadium}$.
$(2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

We need to find an integer $x$ that satisfies this equation.
Let's check for $x=1$.
$2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$.
$2^{31} = 2^{31} - 1$ is not true.
However, if we consider that at 30th insertion it is half full, and we want to find how many more insertions to fill it.
At insertion 31, we add $2^{30}$ balls. The current volume is half full, which is $(2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$. The volume added in the next insertion is $2^{30} \times V_{ball}$.
The new total volume after 31 insertions is $(2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} + 2^{30} \times V_{ball} = (2^{30} - 1 + 2^{30}) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
We know that $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
So, $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times (2^{30} - 1) + 2 - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times (2^{30} - 1) + 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium} + V_{ball}$.
After 31 insertions, the volume is $V_{stadium} + V_{ball}$, which means the stadium is filled and slightly overfilled by one golf ball volume.
Since we need to "fill it", and after 1 more insertion it is filled (and slightly overfilled), the number of insertions left to fill it is 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?1?Let $V$ be the total volume of the stadium.
Let $v = 40 \text{ cm}^3$ be the volume of a single golf ball.
In the $n$-th insertion, $2^{n-1}$ golf balls are inserted.
The total number of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$N_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = \frac{1 \cdot (2^n - 1)}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume occupied by golf balls after $n$ insertions is $V_n = N_n \cdot v = (2^n - 1) \cdot v$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So,
$V_{30} = \frac{V}{2} = (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v$.
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is $V = 2 \cdot V_{30} = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions. Then the total number of insertions is $30 + x$. We want to find $x$ such that the volume occupied after $30+x$ insertions is equal to the full volume $V$.
$V_{30+x} = V$
$(2^{30+x} - 1) \cdot v = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v$
Divide both sides by $v$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

We need to find an integer $x$ that satisfies this equation.
Let's consider integer values for $x$.
If $x=1$, then $30+x = 31$, and $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \cdot v$.
We want to check if $V_{31} = V$.
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \cdot v$
$V = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v = (2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2) \cdot v = (2^{31} - 2) \cdot v$
Comparing $V_{31}$ and $V$:
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \cdot v$
$V = (2^{31} - 2) \cdot v$
$V_{31} > V$.
So, after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfull.

However, we are looking for the number of insertions *left* to fill it, starting from the 30th insertion being half full. Since one more insertion makes it slightly overfull, and at 30th insertion it is half full, it implies that just one more insertion is needed to fill it.  The question likely implies the minimum number of insertions to reach or exceed full capacity. As insertion 31 makes it slightly over full, and insertion 30 is half full, the number of insertions left to fill it is just 1.

Number of insertions left = 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, and $V_{stadium}$ be the volume of the stadium.
The number of balls inserted in the $i$-th insertion is $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $T_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2-1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = T_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
So, $V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions left to fill the stadium. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed. Then we will have a total of $30 + x$ insertions.
The volume of balls after $30 + x$ insertions is $V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) V_{ball}$.
We want to find the smallest integer $x$ such that $V_{30+x} \ge V_{stadium}$.
$(2^{30+x} - 1) V_{ball} \ge (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$ (since $V_{ball} > 0$):
$2^{30+x} - 1 \ge 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^{30+x} \ge 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^{30+x} \ge 2^{31} - 1$.

Let's test $x=1$:
$2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$.
Is $2^{31} \ge 2^{31} - 1$ Yes, $2^{31} > 2^{31} - 1$.
So, with $x=1$ additional insertion, the stadium is at least full.

Let's test $x=0$:
$2^{30+0} = 2^{30}$.
Is $2^{30} \ge 2^{31} - 1$ No, $2^{30} < 2^{31} - 1$.
So, 0 additional insertions is not enough.

Therefore, the minimum number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium is 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let V be the total volume of the stadium.
Let $V_n$ be the volume occupied by golf balls after n insertions.
In the first insertion, 1 ball is inserted, in the second 2 balls, in the third 4 balls, and so on. In the nth insertion, $2^{n-1}$ balls are inserted.
The volume of each golf ball is $v = 40 cm^3$.
After n insertions, the total number of balls inserted is $1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{n-1} = \sum_{i=0}^{n-1} 2^i = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
The volume occupied after n insertions is $V_n = (2^n - 1)v$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
So, $V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1)v = \frac{V}{2}$.
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is $V = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)v = (2^{31} - 2)v$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let's say we need a total of N insertions to fill the stadium.
Then, the volume occupied after N insertions should be equal to the full volume of the stadium, V.
$V_N = (2^N - 1)v = V = (2^{31} - 2)v$.
Divide both sides by v:
$2^N - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^N = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^N = 2^{31} - 1$.

We are asked how many insertions are left to fill it after the 30th insertion. Let x be the number of additional insertions needed. Then $N = 30 + x$.
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$.
We can observe that if $x = 1$, then $2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$.
$2^{31}$ is very close to $2^{31} - 1$.
Since $2^{31} > 2^{31} - 1$, it means that $30+1 = 31$ insertions is slightly more than needed to fill the stadium exactly to the full volume as calculated.
However, since the number of balls must be an integer and the volume is increasing with each insertion, we need to find the smallest integer x such that the stadium is at least full.
Since at 30 insertions it is half full, and at 31 insertions the volume becomes $(2^{31} - 1)v$, which is slightly larger than the full volume $V = (2^{31} - 2)v$, it means that 1 more insertion is enough to fill the stadium.

Number of insertions left = $N - 30 = (30+x) - 30 = x$.
From approximation, $x \approx 1$. Let's check if x=1 is indeed the answer.
If we add 1 more insertion after 30 insertions, we will have $30+1=31$ insertions.
Volume after 31 insertions is $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1)v = (2^{31} - 1)v$.
Full volume is $V = (2^{31} - 2)v$.
Since $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1)v > (2^{31} - 2)v = V$, the stadium is filled (and slightly overfilled) after 31 insertions.
Therefore, starting from the 30th insertion, we need 1 more insertion to fill the stadium.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?
